# HireX Master Project Reverse Engineering & Knowledge Documentation

Generated on: 2026-06-23 22:57:36

This document is the single-source technical knowledge report for the HireX codebase. It was generated by scanning the actual repository files, Python AST structures, frontend source files, model definitions, API decorators, migrations, tests, scripts, reports, storage artifacts, and documentation assets.

## 1. Project Overview

HireX is an HRTech recruitment automation platform. Its current production-MVP focus is candidate sourcing through Excel or imported resume pools, pre-screen validation against job requirements, reusable rejected-pool metadata, batch-based tracking, HR review decisions, and operational dashboards. The long-term architecture extends this into R1 behavioral screening, T1/T2 technical interviews, integrity monitoring, intelligence dashboards, and HR co-pilot insights.

Core business problem: recruiters spend too much time manually collecting resumes, matching candidates to roles, reviewing incomplete information, repeating screening across batches, and losing track of reusable candidate metadata. HireX improves this by storing a candidate master database, validating candidates against job descriptions, preserving rejected/held/shortlisted history by batch, and keeping candidate profiles fresh over time.


Important folders:

- `hirex/`: FastAPI backend, models, services, repositories, validator, Excel intake, taxonomy, database configuration.
- `frontend/`: Next.js HR/admin/candidate UI.
- `alembic/`: Database schema history from foundation through candidate intelligence layer.
- `tests/`: Backend validation, scoring, dashboard, talent pool, workbook, and model tests.
- `scripts/`: Operational scripts for data generation, intake, reset, audit, bootstrap, and verification.
- `storage/`: Local candidate pools, requirements, shortlisted/rejected outputs, freshness cycles.
- `Reports/`: Execution reports, diagrams, project documents, generated workbooks, and decision records.
- `Resumes/`: Real resume inputs and taxonomy/seed references.

## 3. Technology Stack and Dependencies

Backend dependencies are declared in `pyproject.toml` and `requirements.txt`. The production core is FastAPI, SQLAlchemy async ORM, Alembic, Pydantic settings, PostgreSQL asyncpg, JWT auth, pandas/openpyxl, rapidfuzz and scikit-learn.

`pyproject.toml` size: 41 lines. `requirements.txt` size: 66 lines.

Frontend dependencies from `frontend/package.json`: `@types/node`, `@types/react`, `@types/react-dom`, `autoprefixer`, `axios`, `eslint`, `lucide-react`, `next`, `postcss`, `react`, `react-dom`, `react-hook-form`, `server-only`, `tailwindcss`, `typescript`, `typescript-eslint`

The backend uses asynchronous SQLAlchemy sessions and FastAPI dependency injection. The frontend uses Next.js App Router with client screens under `frontend/src`. The system uses PostgreSQL for relational persistence, local Excel files for MVP sourcing, and local report/storage folders for auditability.

## 4. Application Architecture

Current implemented flow:

```text
Candidate Excel / Resume Pool
        -> Job Requirement Excel / JD Management
        -> Excel Intake Service
        -> Candidate Identity Deduplication
        -> Validator Service
        -> Batch Membership + Validator Result
        -> HR Operations Dashboard
        -> R1 Shortlist / HR Review / Held / Rejected
        -> Reusable Talent Pool + Freshness Timeline
```

Planned full flow:

```text
External Sources
  -> Sourcing Batch
  -> Candidate Master Profile
  -> Pre-Screen Validator
  -> R1 Behavioral Agent
  -> HR Gate 1
  -> T1 Technical Agent
  -> HR Gate 2
  -> T2 Advanced Technical Agent
  -> HR Gate 3
  -> Final Decision
  -> Master Intelligence + Pool Analytics
```

Main architectural decisions:

- Candidate data is stored once in the candidate master and reused across batches.
- Every validation run creates batch provenance so results are not confused with all-time totals.
- Rejected candidates are not discarded; they become reusable metadata for future openings.
- Refresh/change detection supports updated candidate profiles without duplicating identities.
- HR retains final control; automation proposes decisions and evidence.

## 5. Database Design and Models

### `Application` table `applications`
File: `hirex/models/application.py`
- `application_id: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(`
- `candidate_id: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(`
- `job_id: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(String(36), ForeignKey("jobs.job_id"), index=True)`
- `application_status: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(String(80), nullable=False, default="Applied")`
- `intake_source: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(String(40), nullable=False, default="candidate_portal")`
- `intake_batch_id: Mapped[str | None] = mapped_column(String(36), index=True)`
- `applied_at: Mapped[datetime] = mapped_column(DateTime(timezone=True), default=datetime.utcnow)`
- `candidate = relationship("CandidateProfile", back_populates="applications")`
- `job = relationship("Job", back_populates="applications")`

### `Resume` table `resumes`
File: `hirex/models/resume.py`
- `resume_id: Mapped[str] = mapped_column(String(36), primary_key=True, default=lambda: str(uuid4()))`

Entity relationship summary:

```text
users
  -> candidate_profiles
candidate_profiles
  -> candidate_identities
  -> candidate_source_records
  -> candidate_refresh_changes
  -> candidate_lifecycle_events
  -> resumes
  -> applications
  -> validator_results
  -> candidate_batch_memberships
jobs
  -> applications
  -> parsed_job_descriptions
  -> validator_results
excel_intake_batches / sourcing_batches
  -> candidate_batch_memberships
  -> validator_results
hr_review_actions
  -> candidate_profiles
  -> validator_results
```

## 6. API Documentation

Detailed API interview/reference document: `Reports/api_endpoint_integration_and_concepts_guide.md`.

HireX currently exposes **41 total backend endpoints**: **40 `/api/*` product endpoints** plus **1 `/health` endpoint**. The API layer is registered in `hirex/main.py` with `app.include_router(...)`. Each router maps one product area to a URL prefix:

- `/api/auth`: login, token, current user, bootstrap manager.
- `/api/candidates`: candidate profile read/update.
- `/api/resumes`: resume upload/list.
- `/api/jobs`: job CRUD.
- `/api/applications`: apply and list applications.
- `/api/admin`: HR operations dashboard, candidate evidence, decisions, analytics.
- `/api/validator`: direct validation, result lookup, R1 queue.
- `/api/excel-intake`: JD configuration, validator batch run, batch list/delete.
- `/api/talent-pool`: reusable candidate pool, batch memberships, stage decisions.

Frontend integration starts from `frontend/src/api/client.ts`. That Axios client sets `baseURL` to `http://127.0.0.1:8000/api` by default and uses a request interceptor to attach `Authorization: Bearer <hirex_token>` to authenticated requests. Therefore, a frontend call such as `apiClient.get("/admin/candidates")` becomes `GET http://127.0.0.1:8000/api/admin/candidates`.

The most important current API process is the HR validator run:

```text
OperationsDashboardPage.runIntake()
  -> optional POST /api/talent-pool/screen
  -> POST /api/excel-intake/run
  -> ExcelIntakeService.run()
  -> CandidateIdentityService resolves/deduplicates candidates
  -> ValidatorService evaluates candidate/JD fit
  -> BatchTrackingService records membership
  -> AdminDashboardService serves dashboard counts, candidate rows, and evidence
```

The dashboard load process is:

```text
OperationsDashboardPage opens
  -> GET /api/excel-intake/configuration
  -> GET /api/excel-intake/batches
  -> GET /api/talent-pool/summary
  -> GET /api/admin/pool-analytics
  -> GET /api/admin/reason-bank
  -> GET /api/admin/summary
  -> GET /api/admin/candidates
```

The candidate review process is:

```text
HR opens candidate
  -> GET /api/admin/candidates/{application_id}?validator_result_id=...
  -> HR checks resume sections, score evidence, missing skills, timeline
  -> POST /api/admin/candidates/{application_id}/decision for REVIEW candidates
  -> HRReviewAction and CandidateBatchMembership are updated
```

Key API concepts used in the project:

- **Endpoint**: one method and URL, such as `POST /api/excel-intake/run`.
- **Router**: FastAPI group of endpoints, such as `hirex/api/admin/routes.py`.
- **Path parameter**: value inside the URL, such as `{application_id}`.
- **Query parameter**: filter after `?`, such as `batch_id` or `validator_result_id`.
- **Request body/payload**: JSON sent to POST/PATCH/PUT endpoints.
- **Response model**: Pydantic schema that controls returned JSON.
- **Dependency injection**: FastAPI provides `current_user` and database `session`.
- **Axios interceptor**: frontend automatically attaches JWT token to requests.
- **Promise/async/await**: frontend and backend wait for API/database work without blocking the whole app.
- **Dynamic rendering**: React updates UI when API responses update state.

- `POST` `"/bulk-evaluate", response_model=BulkEvaluateResponse, status_code=201` -> `bulk_evaluate()`

API behavior summary:

- Auth routes create users, login, issue JWT tokens, and bootstrap manager/admin access.
- Candidate, resume, job, and application routes provide the foundation workflow.
- Validator routes evaluate candidates and expose validation results.
- Excel-intake routes run JD/candidate-pool validation batches, manage requirements, and delete batches.
- Admin routes power HR operations, candidate detail views, decisions, pool analytics, reason bank, and sourcing batch views.
- Talent-pool routes expose reusable pool, batch membership, stale profile, and stage transition operations.

## 7. Service Layer and Business Logic

Services are the system’s business boundary. They keep route handlers thin and centralize decisions.

- `AuthService`: user registration/login, password verification, token subject flow.
- `CandidateService`: candidate profile creation and updates.
- `ResumeService`: upload and resume metadata handling.
- `JobService`: job creation/listing.
- `ApplicationService`: candidate-job application records.
- `ExcelIntakeService`: reads workbooks, validates configuration, creates batches, deduplicates candidates, calls the validator, exports output workbooks, and inserts results.
- `ValidatorService`: parses resume/JD text, calculates component scores, generates evidence, applies thresholds, and persists validator results.
- `AdminDashboardService`: aggregates HR dashboard metrics, candidate lists, detailed evidence, HR actions, reason bank, sourcing batches, and pool analytics.
- `TalentPoolService`: manages reusable candidates, stale profile flags, pool-first screening, and candidate/batch membership.
- `BatchTrackingService`: records candidate stage membership and HR stage decisions.
- `CandidateIdentityService`: avoids duplicate candidate profiles by matching identity keys and source records.

- Lines: 17

Frontend flow:

- `frontend/app` defines Next.js pages and workspace routing.
- `AppShell` provides sidebar navigation and layout.
- `OperationsDashboardPage` is the main HR operations surface for JD selection, intake execution, batch-specific metrics, candidate review, scoring evidence, and HR decisions.
- `BatchesPage` gives batch-level visibility and management.
- Auth screens use the shared Axios client and local token storage.

## 10. Authentication and Authorization

HireX uses JWT-based auth with backend password hashing through `passlib` and token handling through `python-jose`. Frontend stores the returned access token in local storage and sends it through the API client. Admin/HR access is enforced by backend dependencies and route protection. Candidate self-service exists in the foundation, but the current MVP focus is HR/admin operations.

## 11. AI / ML / Validator Logic

Validator modules:

- `resume_parser.py`: extracts resume sections and normalizes candidate information.
- `skill_matcher.py`: compares candidate skills with required/preferred skills.
- `experience_matcher.py`: evaluates experience range fit.
- `education_matcher.py`: checks education requirements.
- `keyword_matcher.py`: computes JD/resume keyword overlap.
- `scoring.py`: combines component scores into a final validator score.
- `decision_engine.py`: maps score and evidence to PASS/REVIEW/FAIL.
- `threshold_engine.py`: supports configurable pass/review thresholds.
- `explanations.py`: creates structured reasons for HR and rejected candidates.
- `service.py`: orchestrates parsing, scoring, version tagging, persistence, and lifecycle events.

The validator is intentionally explainable. A candidate’s outcome is not only a score; it includes matched skills, missing skills, component scores, threshold decision, and reason-bank codes.

## 12. Agent and Automation Readiness

Current implemented automation ends at pre-screen validation and HR decision support. The architecture is ready for:

- R1 behavioral screening agent.
- T1 technical adaptive interview agent.
- T2 advanced technical/system-design agent.
- Integrity monitor for passive signals.
- Master intelligence engine for capacity, forecasting, knowledge graph, and question ROI.
- HR co-pilot for recommendations and red flags.

The important current readiness point is that validator output is structured enough to feed agents with candidate profile, resume evidence, JD fit, missing skills, and decision context.

## 13. Background Jobs, Async Tasks, and Scheduling

The codebase is async-first at the API/database level. Celery and Redis are listed in requirements for future queue/background execution, but the current MVP mainly runs intake and validation synchronously through API calls or scripts. Periodic refresh is modeled at the data level through candidate freshness fields and refresh change records. A production version should schedule refresh jobs every 30 days or source-specific windows.

## 14. Configuration and Environment

Important configuration files:

- `hirex/config/settings.py`: central backend settings.
- `hirex/database/session.py`: async session and engine creation.
- `alembic.ini` and `alembic/env.py`: database migration configuration.
- `frontend/tsconfig.json`, `frontend/next.config.mjs`, `frontend/eslint.config.js`, `frontend/tailwind.config.js`: frontend compiler/build/lint styling configuration.
- `.gitignore`: source control exclusions.

## 15. DevOps and Deployment

Local MVP deployment:

```powershell
uvicorn hirex.main:app --reload --host 127.0.0.1 --port 8000
cd frontend
npm run dev
```

Migration flow:

```powershell
alembic upgrade head
```

Verification flow:

```powershell
pytest -q
cd frontend
npm run build
```

Future deployment should separate API, frontend, PostgreSQL, object storage, queue workers, and monitoring.

## 16. Testing Strategy

Tests cover authentication, models, jobs/applications, resume handling, validator scoring, thresholds, taxonomy, Excel intake, admin dashboard, talent pool, and workbook audits. The test suite proves the critical pieces of the MVP: candidate ingestion, scoring, batch handling, reusable pool behavior, and dashboard outputs.

## 17. Data Flow and Sequence Diagrams

Validator intake sequence:

```text
HR selects JD and candidate source
  -> Frontend calls /api/excel-intake/run
  -> ExcelIntakeService loads JD and candidates
  -> CandidateIdentityService deduplicates profiles
  -> ValidatorService scores each candidate
  -> ValidatorRepository persists results
  -> BatchTrackingService records membership
  -> Dashboard reloads batch-specific metrics
```

Rejected pool reuse:

```text
Candidate fails or is rejected by HR
  -> Lifecycle event records reason
  -> Candidate remains in master database
  -> Future job opens
  -> Pool-first validation reuses matching stored candidates
  -> If target count is short, new sourcing batch can be added
```

Freshness sequence:

```text
Source refresh imports candidate
  -> Identity service finds existing candidate
  -> Refresh change detection compares skills/resume/profile fields
  -> Candidate master is updated without duplicate profile
  -> Timeline records what changed and when
  -> Future validator run uses fresh profile
```

## 18. Design Patterns and Architecture Principles

- Router-service-repository separation.
- Async database session dependency injection.
- SQLAlchemy declarative model layer.
- Alembic migration history as schema contract.
- DTO/schema boundary through Pydantic.
- Batch provenance for auditable decisions.
- Idempotent candidate identity handling.
- Explainable scoring over black-box decisions.
- Local Excel storage as MVP adapter, replaceable later by Naukri/LinkedIn/company portal connectors.

## 19. Security Analysis

Implemented controls:

- Password hashing.
- JWT access tokens.
- Authenticated HR/admin operations.
- Separation of backend routes by domain.
- Database-managed IDs and foreign keys.

Risks to address before production:

- Local storage token handling should move toward secure cookies or hardened token lifecycle.
- Resume uploads and external scraped content must be treated as untrusted input.
- Role-based authorization should be expanded beyond basic manager/admin checks.
- PII retention policy and consent/audit requirements must be defined.
- External scraping must follow platform terms, legal review, and rate-limiting.

## 20. Performance and Scalability

Current MVP is suitable for local batch validation of hundreds to thousands of rows. Scaling improvements:

- Move validation batches to queue workers.
- Add pagination and indexed batch/candidate queries.
- Store large resumes/audio/video in object storage.
- Cache taxonomy and repeated JD parsing.
- Add vector search for semantic role matching.
- Track validator runtime per candidate and batch.
- Add database indexes for candidate identity, batch membership, status, and job role filters.

## 22. Project Defense Guide

How to explain HireX to a mentor:

HireX is not only a resume sorter. It is a recruitment operating system that builds a reusable candidate database. Every candidate is stored once, every validation run is tracked by batch, every decision is explainable, and rejected candidates remain useful for future roles after profile refresh.

Why Excel is used now:

Excel is the MVP intake adapter. It lets HR test role requirements and candidate pools immediately. The same intake contract can later be replaced by LinkedIn, Naukri, company portals, ATS integrations, or upload panels without changing the core validator and talent-pool architecture.

Why rejected candidates are stored:

Rejected does not mean useless forever. A candidate may be weak for one role, strong for another role, or stronger after learning new skills. Storing metadata with lifecycle events gives the company a growing private talent pool.

Why batch-level views matter:

All-time counts can mislead HR. Each hiring run must show its own evaluated, pass, review, rejected, held, and moved-forward numbers. Global pool analytics should be separate.

Why freshness matters:

Candidate profiles change over time. A 30-day refresh cycle or source-based refresh process updates skills, projects, certifications, and resume text without duplicating the candidate identity.

## 24. Executive Summary

HireX currently implements a strong MVP foundation for HRTech candidate intake, validation, batch tracking, reusable rejected-pool metadata, freshness/change detection, dashboard review, and PostgreSQL-backed persistence. The strongest architectural choices are candidate identity deduplication, batch-specific results, explainable scoring, and future-safe source adapters. The next strongest improvements are queue-based validation, production-grade RBAC, source connector compliance, and agent execution for R1/T1/T2 interview rounds.
